  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_203206bf-2196-49aa-9030-1e0ab5f03763'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText8100661009245803118" style="display:none">This didn't excite me as much as its predecessor, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13836.Wild_Magic__Immortals___1_" title="Wild Magic (Immortals, #1) by Tamora Pierce" rel="nofollow noopener">Wild Magic</a>, primarily for the following reason:<br /><br />Daine and Numair are in the forest then<br />Daine enters into the mind of an animal.<br />Daine and Numair and some wolves are in the forest then<br />Daine enters into the mind of an animal.<br />Daine and Numair go to a castle then<br />Daine enters into the mind of an animal.<br />Daine hangs out with wolves and then<br />Daine enters into the mind of an animal.<br />Daine meets some immortals, good and bad, and then<br />Daine enters into the mind of an animal.<br />Daine enters into the mind of an animal to talk to Numair through a barrier.<br />Daine is always tired because it takes a lot of energy when<br />Daine enters into the mind of an animal.<br />Daine enters into the mind of an animals to go everywhere, all the time, forever and ever amen. <br /><br />Okay, that's it, you get the point. I still love Tamora Pierce and I'll still keep going with the series because I like the world.</span>

<div id="review_1566065581" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1566065581" />
    <a title="Madeline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111921-madeline"><img alt="Madeline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1220803522p2/111921.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1566065581?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madeline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madeline" href="/user/show/111921-madeline">Madeline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1566065581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16726565350879984443">It's been over a year since I read the first book in Tamora Pierce's <i>Immortals</i> quartet, <i>Wild Magic</i>. I remember enjoying it almost more than Pierce's Alanna books (which will always be first in my heart, of course) but other than that, I started this book with only vague memories of the plot and characters of the previous installment. <br/><br/>Luckily, there's not much to catch up on - Pierce's novels are characterized by fast-paced action, a relatively small and memorable cast of characters, and fairly s</span>
  <span id="freeText16726565350879984443" style="display:none">It's been over a year since I read the first book in Tamora Pierce's <i>Immortals</i> quartet, <i>Wild Magic</i>. I remember enjoying it almost more than Pierce's Alanna books (which will always be first in my heart, of course) but other than that, I started this book with only vague memories of the plot and characters of the previous installment. <br /><br />Luckily, there's not much to catch up on - Pierce's novels are characterized by fast-paced action, a relatively small and memorable cast of characters, and fairly simple conflicts and plots. And Pierce does a good job of giving the reader enough backstory and reminders from the first book, so even if you're like me and are resuming this series after a long absence, you should be fine.<br /><br />As is also the case with Pierce's books, there is almost no setup - <i>Wolf-Speaker</i> starts practically in the middle of the action, with a wolf pack (the same pack who Daine briefly ran with after her mother's death, when she nearly lost her own sense of humanity) contacting our heroine and asking for help. The pack's habitat is being threatened by human development, and they want her to intercede for them. Meanwhile, the rulers who control the land where the wolves live are also plotting against the king of Tortall, and let's not forget that the Immortals (powerful ancient monsters/gods who recently got released into the world) are quietly and not-so-quietly moving around the country.<br /><br />Reading this book gave me strong flashbacks to <i>The Woman Who Rides Like a Man</i>, the third book in the Alanna series. I still consider it the weakest of the series, because after the absolutely breakneck pace of the previous books, this one seemed to move at a snail's pace while we watch Alanna hanging around in the desert and helping a local tribe. <i>Wolf-Speaker</i> suffers from the same problem - despite the fact that there's plenty of conflict, everything feels <i>so slow</i>. There's also a lot of repetition, because this book has Daine experimenting with her powers and learning to enter animals' minds, and it means that we have to read essentially the same scene over and over as she practices this skill on various animals. This repetition works for younger readers, but I was pretty bored for most of the book.<br /><br />The conflict itself - rebellion against the king, aided by Immortals - isn't very interesting either, mainly because we're meeting the antagonists for the first time in this book, and the fact that Daine spends most of her time with the wolf pack means that the bad guys never get to do much. Failing to properly develop the villains, and removing Daine from the action for the majority of the book, means that the stakes never feel as high as they should. <br /><br />Not that I disliked the book, overall. The fact that most of the characters are animals, each with their own personalities and conflicts, would have delighted me if I'd read this book as a child. Pierce is particularly good at coming up with animal names, and if you manage to get through this entire story without falling head-over-heels in love with Quickmunch the marmot, then I don't know what to do with you. I liked the wolf pack, and child readers will have more fun reading about them than I did - it's hard to get too invested in these characters when you know they're just a detour on the way to the main action. <br /><br />Although the Alanna and the Daine stories have a lot in common, the series are trying to accomplish very different things, which becomes clear in <i>Wolf-Speaker</i>. Alanna's adventures were all about teaching girls that their gender doesn't stop them from being whatever they want to be, and that they can accomplish anything through determination and hard work. Daine's books teach children that the world isn't black and white, and that you can't make judgements about people (or in this case, creatures) based on what they are or where they come from.<br /><br />In the Alanna books, the villains are not complex, and everyone pretty much adheres to their assigned roles - if someone is a bad guy in Book One, they're going to be a bad guy in Book Four - and the lines are pretty clearly drawn. Daine's journey, it seems, is shaping up to be a little more complex than that. In the first book, we established that many of the Immortals, like the Stormwings, are evil and scary. In the second book, Daine and the reader are forced to reconsider that idea, and realize that all Immortals are not alike. Just because they're a Stormwing, Daine learns, you can't assume they're evil. Here's a scene where Iakoju, an ogre, lays it out clearly for the readers:<br /><br />"Maura frowned. 'I don't understand. If you're peaceful - if you really only like to farm - how come you're called "ogres"? Ogres are monsters, aren't they? And how come your people are always fighting with ours?'<br />'We are big,' replied Iajoku quietly. 'Ugly. Our color different from men color. No all ogres are same, either. Some take what they want. Some fight with men. My people, kin clans, we only like farming, not fighting. Some ogres only like fighting. Are all men the same?'"<br /><br />This is a suprisingly complex concept for a kids' series, especially since fantasy audiences are trained to think of all evil-inclined creatures as one singular hive-mind (Tolkien, bless him, assured us that orcs are pure evil and that's that, and I think it set an unfortunate precedent in fantasy), and it's really the only thing that saved this book for me - I'm looking forward to continuing this series, just to see how Pierce continues to develop this idea.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16726565350879984443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2586664378" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2586664378?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/39857741-wolf-speaker">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=fantastic-fabrications">fantastic-fabrications</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2586664378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4596031654900650145">It is hard not to fall head over heels in love with a book that involves animals such as a dragon called Kitten, a wolf pup called Silly, and a hound called Prettyfoot. What is hard to do is combine these beloved creatures inside of a plot that delivers as much intrigue as it does adorable creatures, and as much authenticity as it does no-hold-bars belief in its creations. However, Pierce does all that with ease.<br/><br/>The first book in the Immortals series introduced the reader to central character, D</span>
  <span id="freeText4596031654900650145" style="display:none">It is hard not to fall head over heels in love with a book that involves animals such as a dragon called Kitten, a wolf pup called Silly, and a hound called Prettyfoot. What is hard to do is combine these beloved creatures inside of a plot that delivers as much intrigue as it does adorable creatures, and as much authenticity as it does no-hold-bars belief in its creations. However, Pierce does all that with ease.<br /><br />The first book in the Immortals series introduced the reader to central character, Daine, and her wild magic abilities. The story was a fun, straight-forward adventure story and I adored it for that. In this second instalment however, the political stakes have been heightened and the story-line become more convoluted. With it, the reader is allowed to traverse through previously unseen segments of this vast world, explore more aspects of the unique magic system, and also see Daine begin to grow into the fierce, strong, and proud individual we already saw inklings of her becoming, in the first book.<br /><br />I only grew more enraptured as the story progressed and only more attached to these characters as their continued survival seemed more precarious. I may be new to discovering the wonder that is Tamora Pierce but I am now a life-long fan, after discovering this series.<br /><br />I received a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. Thank you to the author, Tamora Pierce, and the publisher, Harper Voyager, for this opportunity.</span>

<div id="review_2602802433" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2602802433" />
    <a title="Lady Clementina ffinch-ffarowmore" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore"><img alt="Lady Clementina ffinch-ffarowmore" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560079929p2/5917681.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2602802433?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady Clementina ffinch-ffarowmore" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady Clementina ffinch-ffarowmore" href="/user/show/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore">Lady Clementina ffinch-ffarowmore</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore?shelf=american">american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore?shelf=animals">animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore?shelf=tamora-pierce">tamora-pierce</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2602802433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18401123162217985765">My thanks to Harper Collins UK and NetGalley for a review copy of this one.<br/><br/>This is the second of the Immortals series (my review of book 1 is here:<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2598286242?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1'>https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a>) by Tamora Pierce. The one opens with the wolves that Daine once hunted with trying to reach her and thinking over the news they’ve received of her from other creatures of the forest. Daine, now fourteen, meanwhile is heading with her mentor/teacher, the mage Numair Salmalin, their horses including Cloud, and K</span>
  <span id="freeText18401123162217985765" style="display:none">My thanks to Harper Collins UK and NetGalley for a review copy of this one.<br /><br />This is the second of the Immortals series (my review of book 1 is here:<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2598286242?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a>) by Tamora Pierce. The one opens with the wolves that Daine once hunted with trying to reach her and thinking over the news they’ve received of her from other creatures of the forest. Daine, now fourteen, meanwhile is heading with her mentor/teacher, the mage Numair Salmalin, their horses including Cloud, and Kitten the dragon baby, towards the pack for they have sent for her help as their new home, Dunlath is in trouble. The two-feet there are cutting down all the trees, mining incessantly, chasing away prey making the place unliveable for them, and ultimately for themselves. When they get there however, they find that it isn’t only the animals who are in trouble. A family of local nobles, the lords of Dunlath, are plotting treason against King Jonathan, and switching loyalties. Here they are aided by a whole group of rogue mages, who have some very powerful magic at their command, and don’t seem to care who or what they destroy. Circumstances become such that Daine is left all alone with only her animal friends and some immortal ones in Dunlath. The only other human helping her at first is ten-year-old Lady Maura, younger sister of the Lady Yolane. Daine begins to learn and practice more of what her wild magic makes her capable of, and these new found powers and her friends are what help her face and defeat the “villains” of the piece. <br /><br />If anything, I think I enjoyed this one even more than the first book. The first book obviously had to set out the background, and introduce us to the world that Daine lived in, and the friends she found in Tortall, but this one to me felt more rounded as a story. I enjoyed watching Daine, who spends much of the novel away from human company, explore her new powers or rather the new uses she discovers of her magic. This helps her not only to do things she couldn’t earlier but view the world through the perspectives of her different animal friends. This was an element I really enjoyed. Pierce does a great job of highlighting the various things—sounds, smells, sights—that different animals would notice, and making one (even the reader) feel that they were looking through the eyes and mind of the animal in question. The adventure elements for me were fairly exciting as well. But besides these, the book also had some important messages to give. It may be set in a fantasy world, but even there “humans” continue to behave as they do in real life, destroying their environment, surroundings, disrespecting other living creatures for what they think is their own gain. The other was about needing to understand creatures/life that is different, human or animal, as life, as creatures/people who have thoughts, feelings, concerns, and who shouldn’t be judged as monsters or evil in an off-handed way. Here Maura, who is scared of some of Daine’s “friends” manages to shows Daine how she herself might be prejudiced unfairly against some others. Pierce manages to show us that even people who are “good” aren’t always flawless and may have their own prejudices and discriminatory attitudes that they need to address—another message extremely relevant for our world. Once again a wonderful read, in which I especially enjoyed all the animals and Daine’s interactions with them! <br /><br />This review appears on my blog here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://potpourri2015.wordpress.com/2018/11/30/review-wolf-speaker-by-tamora-pierce/">https://potpourri2015.wordpress.com/2...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="18401123162217985765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_200062578" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/200062578" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/200062578?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781934180365" href="/book/show/1045470.Wolf_speaker">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer200062578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11909289726474787253">If I weren’t writing a review for every single book this year, this would definitely be one that I would skip. This is a clear transition book and I really don’t have much to say about it. I liked it; I didn’t love it. I never felt annoyed, bored, moved, or enthusiastic about this book. I listened to it while running errands and doing some cleaning and it was the perfect background. <br/> <br/>Daine’s wolf pack family, who gave her a home when she was lost, has called for help. Their valley is being torn </span>
  <span id="freeText11909289726474787253" style="display:none">If I weren’t writing a review for every single book this year, this would definitely be one that I would skip. This is a clear transition book and I really don’t have much to say about it. I liked it; I didn’t love it. I never felt annoyed, bored, moved, or enthusiastic about this book. I listened to it while running errands and doing some cleaning and it was the perfect background. <br /> <br />Daine’s wolf pack family, who gave her a home when she was lost, has called for help. Their valley is being torn apart by loggers and hunters and will soon be destroyed. Daine vows to try, even though as a child, there is little that she can do. But there may be more at work in the valley than simple human greed. A group of the King’s Riders has also gone missing, and Daine soon finds the source of the treachery. Along the way, Daine discovers new powers with <i>interesting</i> side-effects. Despite her young age, she may be the only person who can set things right.<br /><br />Daine is fourteen years old in this second installment, and like every teenager on the planet, she thinks that she knows everything. She’s opinionated and quick to judge. But this passion of conviction also gives her the strength to stand up and make a plea for the valley, in the face of ridicule (which is the most satisfying part of this book). Every time Daine lets her preconceived notions blind her, there is someone there to force her to reconsider. And for all of Daine’s stubbornness, she <i>listens.</i><br /><br />Daine spends the vast majority of this book cut off from all of the human characters that I grew to love in <u>Wild Magic</u>, with a cast of animal friends. Although I really love the conflict that arises from Daine’s involvement with the animals (exposure to her magic makes them more and more intelligent and human-like), I just don’t find them as interesting as the human characters. I really missed Numair, Alanna, Onua, and the others. I also really hope that Daine finally learns the identity of her father in the next book. She has received many clues, and I feel that it would be unrealistic for her to take very much longer to figure it out.<br /><br />I really like the direction that this story seems to be taking, with assumed enemies becoming allies and the world proving to be more grey and complicated than Daine realized. I think that realizing that you don’t know a damn thing is an essential part of becoming an adult, and I can’t wait for Daine to get there.<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />The Cranberries – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BTWp46aKrtA" rel="nofollow noopener">Put Me Down</a><br /><br />Daine is a mediator, a bridge between the races. But as a young and inexperienced girl with a magical gift that few believe even exists, she faces a lot of obstacles. This song makes me think of Daine fulfilling her destiny and leading the world to a better place. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11909289726474787253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_34273625" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34273625" />
    <a title="Kogiopsis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis"><img alt="Kogiopsis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494267218p2/1462364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34273625?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kogiopsis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kogiopsis" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis">Kogiopsis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34273625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11334489174177403893">*happy sigh*<br/><br/>I always finish these books with a smile on my face. There's just something about them that leaves me feeling like this:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380317679ra/689464.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>It's hard to write a review for something you love this much. I'd much rather just tell you all to READ IT NAO and let it speak for itself.<br/>But you're not here for that. And this book deserves a proper review from me. I'll try.<br/><br/>First of all, to let some parts of it speak for themselves, here are a few lines of sparkling dialogue from this book, iconified by awesome pe</span>
  <span id="freeText11334489174177403893" style="display:none">*happy sigh*<br><br>I always finish these books with a smile on my face. There's just something about them that leaves me feeling like this:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380317679ra/689464.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>It's hard to write a review for something you love this much. I'd much rather just tell you all to READ IT NAO and let it speak for itself.<br>But you're not here for that. And this book deserves a proper review from me. I'll try.<br><br>First of all, to let some parts of it speak for themselves, here are a few lines of sparkling dialogue from this book, iconified by awesome people who are not me:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317682i/689465.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317682i/689466.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317682i/689467.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Pretty much the whole book is like that. I mean, if you're familiar with Pierce, you know she writes amazingly well, so that's not the center of the show. It's important, though, because no matter how many times I read this book, it always makes me laugh.<br><br><br>Anyhow, I actually don't like Wolf Speaker nearly as much as the other three books in the Immortals series. It might even be a four-star read, if it weren't for two characters: Maura and Rikash.<br><br>Maura is ten, and I always forget that. She's also a lot more sheltered than the kids Daine met at Pirate's Swoop, and though she has maturity, spine, and spunk, she's not quite as open-minded. This is, naturally, a challenge for Daine. I guess the reason I don't like this book too much is that Daine's development is getting over prejudices, and prejudices are often frustrating for me (even though I know I'm prone to them). It was nice, though, that Maura represented a part of the nobility Daine hadn't really encountered much: the kind that doesn't go around kicking ass and taking names and generally being open-minded and awesome in all possible ways. She's not a bad kid - she's intelligent and brave - but she doesn't adapt to some things as easily as other people do. Having her around added another element to the story, because it wasn't just about freeing the valley from the evil nobles. It was also about restoring the valley to the kind of ruler that would treat it right, even if she's only ten. While Maura probably lives out a fairly quiet life in Dunlath and so a book of her adventures is unlikely, I wish we got to see more of her. I think she comes up briefly in one of the Protector of the Small books, but that's it.<br><br>Rikash, on the other hand, we see more of. A lot more. But shh, spoilers! So what I'll content myself by saying is that if you disliked or hated Stormwings after Wild Magic, Rikash will probably change your mind. He might be a Stormwing, but he's also a genuinely good guy. His primary relationship is with Maura, of whom he says "Affection has led me to indulge Lady Maura more than is wise." He's not a monster, which is the point of his presence in the book. (He's also here to say "Get that squirrel!" in hilarious circumstances.)<br><br><br><br>There are other good aspects about this book, of course - some great Numair moments, unique animal characters, a dastardly plot, a magical battle, etcetera. But that's what you can expect from pretty much any book in the quartet. Wolf-Speaker wouldn't really stand out to me without Maura and Rikash; they make it excellent instead of just great.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11334489174177403893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=middle-school">middle-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=alternate-universe">alternate-universe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=magic">magic</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer580507930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4196385512671317506">I think I set my bar so high for this series from the first book that this book was inevitably a letdown. I loved the first book. I loved being introduced to all the characters, I loved learning about Daine's "wild magic" and her journey into self-discovery. Even the lengthy and confusing battle at the end didn't ruin it for me. This book, however, just dragged on. Daine is traveling with her mentor, looking for a missing group of Riders and re-encountering the pack of wolves with whom she bonde</span>
  <span id="freeText4196385512671317506" style="display:none">I think I set my bar so high for this series from the first book that this book was inevitably a letdown. I loved the first book. I loved being introduced to all the characters, I loved learning about Daine's "wild magic" and her journey into self-discovery. Even the lengthy and confusing battle at the end didn't ruin it for me. This book, however, just dragged on. Daine is traveling with her mentor, looking for a missing group of Riders and re-encountering the pack of wolves with whom she bonded and which came to her assistance when she needed it before we were introduced to her in the first book. They were a crucial part in her development, and it was disappointing to me that they were so lacking in character.<br /><br />I found the plot boring and uninspired. Even if I didn't read the first few books in the series, I grew to like the characters from my introduction to them in the first book of the Immortals, and it was to my disappointment that they didn't make an appearance in this one. The mystery was boring, I didn't like the antagonists...before you say, well, no shit, Sherlock. They're supposed to be unlikeable. I mean that they were so...villainous, traditionally so. They were one-dimensional and boring. I also did not like the fact that Daine spends so much of her time interacting with animals. I like human interactions, I like it when Daine is out of her comfort zone. Animals are nice and good, but I'm not a furry. I'm really not into animals as characters. I prefer human interactions, and this book was lacking in that. I'm hoping book 3 will be better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4196385512671317506" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3222095035" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~" href="/user/show/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out">Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781934180600" href="/book/show/7571534-wolf-speaker">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=borrowed-library">borrowed-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=animals-pets">animals-pets</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3222095035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12282031916286836644">This is on me. The writing is as good as ever, and Daine and Numair are still great. Daine even has to figure things out on her own after she's accidentally separated from Numair, and it was really cool to see her grow stronger and more confident in herself and her powers. And so far, there's not even a hint of "romance," much less a love triangle, that made the Alanna quartet a bit of chore to wade through. <br/><br/>But...so many talking animals. And ok, it's only because Daine is able to talk mind to m</span>
  <span id="freeText12282031916286836644" style="display:none">This is on me. The writing is as good as ever, and Daine and Numair are still great. Daine even has to figure things out on her own after she's accidentally separated from Numair, and it was really cool to see her grow stronger and more confident in herself and her powers. And so far, there's not even a hint of "romance," much less a love triangle, that made the Alanna quartet a bit of chore to wade through. <br /><br />But...so many talking animals. And ok, it's only because Daine is able to talk mind to mind with them, they're not actually talking. Most of them aren't, anyway. But my lord. Sometimes I can roll with this and even enjoy it, but this was nonstop and I just couldn't stand it after awhile, even if there were some humorous moments and some interesting world-building going on with it. Also, once again, the villains are super evil. There's never much subtlety when it comes to Pierce's villains or their evil plots. I guess because these are geared for a YA audience, but it does make things predictable. Add on some repetitiveness and this started to drag for me a lot in the second half.<br /><br />I think I'll take a break from this quartet and move onto the next one, which looks like it could be interesting, though I'm hoping it's not too much of a rehash of Alanna.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12282031916286836644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50266440" />
    <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip"><img alt="Jennifer Wardrip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442657515p2/1125613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50266440?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Wardrip" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip">Jennifer Wardrip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50266440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12169992872491387222">Reviewed by Candace Cunard for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>This second book in Tamora Pierce's THE IMMORTALS QUARTET centers around the further development of Daine's magical ability to communicate with animals. <br/><br/>The story begins when the wolf pack that lives near her former home village sends an envoy to ask for her assistance communicating with the humans who are ruining the lands where these wolves hunt. Daine, who owes a debt of gratitude to these wolves for having cared for her once she escaped her vill</span>
  <span id="freeText12169992872491387222" style="display:none">Reviewed by Candace Cunard for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />This second book in Tamora Pierce's THE IMMORTALS QUARTET centers around the further development of Daine's magical ability to communicate with animals. <br /><br />The story begins when the wolf pack that lives near her former home village sends an envoy to ask for her assistance communicating with the humans who are ruining the lands where these wolves hunt. Daine, who owes a debt of gratitude to these wolves for having cared for her once she escaped her village, can't say no to their request, and along with her wizardly teacher, the powerful mage Numair Salmalín, she journeys to Fief Dunlath, the area known by the wolves as Long Lake. <br /><br />There, things are much worse than they initially seemed. Not only are the rulers of Fief Dunlath completely disregarding the impact of their actions upon the local wildlife, but Numair recognizes one of their guests as a Combat Mage from the Carthaki Empire, a country currently engaged in small skirmishes with Tortall. It soon becomes apparent that the Lady of the fief is engaged in double dealings with the Carthakis. <br /><br />While Numair speeds back to warn King Jonathan of what is happening, Daine stays behind with her wolf-friends, gathering information and making plans for putting an end to the mining and garrisoning of soldiers that are destroying the natural habitats of more animals than just the wolves. <br /><br />In a continuation of her skills from the previous book, Daine learns how to share her mind with animals, seeing through their eyes and sensing with their senses. She also discovers, much to her surprise, that any lengthy mental cohabitation could give her unexpected animal characteristics, like the ears of a mouse or the eyes of a hawk, that fade away only after she has detached herself from the animal's consciousness. With the help of a whole network of animal friends, Daine sketches out a plan of attack that will show the nobles of Fief Dunlath what happens when you mess with the wildlife. <br /><br />Overall, I found this book quite enjoyable; the continued development of Daine's character was accomplished smoothly, and the characters newly introduced in this volume were fleshed out in their own rights. Particularly notable characters included, not just Numair, but also the baby dragon Stormsong, known as Kitten, and all of the wolves of the Long Lake pack. <br /><br />If you liked the first book, you'll love the next one! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12169992872491387222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78004651?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kris" href="/user/show/2125614-kris">kris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/7123950-wolf-speaker">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78004651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10629590868092653070">[Also read 17 December 2007]<br/><br/>Daine is summoned by her former Pack to Dunlath where shenanigans are afoot. Once there, she is separated from everyone but her animal pals to stop high treason in its tracks!! (If this sounds like an after school special on PBS, YOU’D BE RIGHT.)<br/><br/>1. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41348530?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>While there have been some very good conversations</a> about the ‘easiness’ Daine experiences in growing her magic, I would argue that the simplicity of the world extends well past just Daine’s magic. For any given conflict, an</span>
  <span id="freeText10629590868092653070" style="display:none">[Also read 17 December 2007]<br /><br />Daine is summoned by her former Pack to Dunlath where shenanigans are afoot. Once there, she is separated from everyone but her animal pals to stop high treason in its tracks!! (If this sounds like an after school special on PBS, YOU’D BE RIGHT.)<br /><br />1. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41348530?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">While there have been some very good conversations</a> about the ‘easiness’ Daine experiences in growing her magic, I would argue that the simplicity of the world extends well past just Daine’s magic. For any given conflict, an easy and simple solution is near at hand. The world itself seems to bend to Daine’s needs so that nothing truly holds any weight. <br /><br />A perfect example: Scrape’s death. I found myself rolling my eyes (instead of being properly horrified because <i>kitty</i>) because OF COURSE Daine has the god’s ears, so OF COURSE the cat was in no danger at all. OF COURSE. <br /><br />Even Numair’s abilities are just tossed into the book—oh yes, <i>once</i> he was a book-smart fool, BUT NOW HE IS THE MOST POWERFUL MAGE IN THE WORLD!! (Seriously, how convenient that he can spot poisons and do adequate shielding spells and know all the words of power and and—<br /><br />2. My complaints over the simplicity extend into the text itself. There were quite a few instances where Pierce chose to frame her narration using a slash (“Leader yipped in apology/agreement”; “Daine gloried in the power of this strange/familiar body”). First, I think this technique could be WONDERFUL in the right setting. BUT THIS WAS NOT IT. Instead of using nuanced writing to convey her meaning, Pierce just tosses both words in there and moves on. It reeks of “I don't care enough to make this world <i>real</i>” and I hate it. <br /><br />3. I sincerely did not care for the majority of Daine’s companions? They’re transient. They’re simple. They offer a mirror for Daine to expand her own consequence and I would rather see the limits of her consequence, to better understand Daine’s place in the world. (I.e., if she can do all things and be all things—what is to stop her? What balances her immense power in the world? (And I know that Pierce would have us believe that Daine is inherently <i>good</i>, but a) that is the easy way out, and b) Pierce DIRECTLY CONTRADICTS IT IN THIS TEXT—that all things are not built for good or evil but for a unique purpose that runs contrary to other living things. This leads me to…)<br /><br />4. The one interesting conflict to be found in this heap of a novel—the questioning of good versus evil and how purpose can manifest itself—is shortchanged, underdeveloped, contradicted, and left out to rot. Daine flips and flops on this issue like a beached mackerel: are the Immortals evil? Immediately after killing a CLEARLY ENSLAVED Hurrock, she speaks to the Stormwings as rational beings. MAKE UP YOUR DAMNED MIND, DAINE.<br /><br />It was kind of appalling in its obliviousness.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10629590868092653070" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30014834-skye?shelf=2-star-did-not-like">2-star-did-not-like</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30014834-skye?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2619654543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11413812116940459406">I received a free ebook version of this from Netgalley. Thankyou to both Netgalley and the publisher for allowing me to read this! My review is still honest.<br/><br/>I'm really sorry to say that I think this book has second book syndrome, and I don't think it's as good as Wild Magic. I am still invested in the series and the characters, and I have high hopes for Emperor Mage, but this one wasn't up to the standard of the first book.<br/>This series is based around a young girl who has wild magic, powers that </span>
  <span id="freeText11413812116940459406" style="display:none">I received a free ebook version of this from Netgalley. Thankyou to both Netgalley and the publisher for allowing me to read this! My review is still honest.<br /><br />I'm really sorry to say that I think this book has second book syndrome, and I don't think it's as good as Wild Magic. I am still invested in the series and the characters, and I have high hopes for Emperor Mage, but this one wasn't up to the standard of the first book.<br />This series is based around a young girl who has wild magic, powers that allow her to communicate with animals in various ways. Immortal creatures who haven't been seen in Tortall for centuries have recently began appearing, and something is amiss.<br />I do really love the magical aspect and the animals, there are some really strong characters that emerge in this way. I especially loved the cats and Flicker, and I enjoyed the wolf pack's dynamic. The introduction of Maura in this one was great as I think she's a very likeable and strong character. I do always love Daine, and Numair is growing on me. Pierce is very creative with the creatures she creates and with her interpretations.<br />I guess for me this one felt a little pointless. I don't yet understand how the events of this one tie in with the overall series arc and the issues that were first presented in Wild Magic, and the action scenes and conclusion paled in comparison to the excellence of the battle in book 1. I didn't feel like that much really happened and it was quite slow for a short book, so I wasn't as enthralled. I'd also call this a middle grade rather than a young adult, as our characters are always very safe and everything is resolved perfectly and wrapped neatly up. I do want a little more angst and danger, and sometimes it's good for things not to go the main character's way.<br />Will I still read Emperor Mage with hope in my heart? Of course! I love these characters and the world, but I am left disappointed with this one in particular.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11413812116940459406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Pierce jumps straight into the story without hardly any background information, so if you are unfamiliar with the fantasy realm of Tortall, I very highly recommend that you don't begin your journey with thi</span>
  <span id="freeText4468322933932214892" style="display:none">Wolf Speaker is the second of Tamora Pierce's "Immortals Quartet" concerning fourteen-year-old Daine, a young woman who possesses "Wild Magic," giving her the ability to communicate with animals, heal any animal wound, and in this book, to gradually change her form into any animal she wishes. Pierce jumps straight into the story without hardly any background information, so if you are unfamiliar with the fantasy realm of Tortall, I very highly recommend that you don't begin your journey with this book: start with Wild Magic, or even better The Lioness Quartet, Pierce's first books concerning Tortall.<br /><br />Daine and her mentor Numair have been sent abroad in order to investigate the disappearance of several of the Queen's Riders, and in doing so Daine...     <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4063913-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351396026p2/4063913.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1974770086044919863">The fun thing about rereading books that you loved when you were younger is that it reminds you how much you used to love them (I'm not sure that sentence makes sense, but let's go with it). This book could have been tailor-made for adolescent-me. I loved Julie of the Wolves, and the idea of JOINING A WOLF PACK AND USING MAGIC POWERS TO TALK TO THEM sounded like the greatest thing in the world. I also really enjoy some of the side characters we meet in this book. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7848377809920237439">I was in the mood for some fairly mindless YA Fantasy today — something heroic and delightful, a tonic to cleanse my palate after the torture that was that Feist <em>Merchant Prince</em> book, which I read yesterday and <em>hated</em> — and this jumped into my hand. I was very quickly re-immersed in the world of Daine, our teenage animal mage, and the imminent threat to the land from a darkness beyond.<br/><br/>This one sees Daine and her mentor Numair caught up in a rebellion against the King, with a sideline of sentient </span>
  <span id="freeText7848377809920237439" style="display:none">I was in the mood for some fairly mindless YA Fantasy today — something heroic and delightful, a tonic to cleanse my palate after the torture that was that Feist <em>Merchant Prince</em> book, which I read yesterday and <em>hated</em> — and this jumped into my hand. I was very quickly re-immersed in the world of Daine, our teenage animal mage, and the imminent threat to the land from a darkness beyond.<br /><br />This one sees Daine and her mentor Numair caught up in a rebellion against the King, with a sideline of sentient wolves and some unexpected complexity given to the “evil” creatures who infest Tortall. The pace is speedy, for the most part, the writing engaging, and lessons are learned left and right as young Daine — still just a tween — ever-so-slowly comes of age in this magical world of wonder and, it must be said, mild terror.<br /><br />Perfectly pleasant, somewhat predictable, easy, simple, fun. This was exactly the book I needed to read today, if not a book I ever really needed to read at all.<br /><br />Huh. Weird.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2788814252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11677920538507898426">Back in the day, this was my least favorite of the series and the only one I didn't reread. But today, honestly, I love it almost as much as the first one. The reason I didn't like it as much was because it's a bit of a departure from the characters I love, Daine spends a lot of this book on her own with animals separated from Numair, and even though he's in it some, he's the only one from previous books to play a major role. I miss the rest of the cast and the normal setting. But that being sai</span>
  <span id="freeText11677920538507898426" style="display:none">Back in the day, this was my least favorite of the series and the only one I didn't reread. But today, honestly, I love it almost as much as the first one. The reason I didn't like it as much was because it's a bit of a departure from the characters I love, Daine spends a lot of this book on her own with animals separated from Numair, and even though he's in it some, he's the only one from previous books to play a major role. I miss the rest of the cast and the normal setting. But that being said, on reread I do really love the story and I love the new cast of all the animals. I think the plot is really strong and I was surprised how much I do love this book.</span>

<div id="review_230425814" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/230425814" />
    <a title="delaney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6270594-delaney"><img alt="delaney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553837637p2/6270594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/230425814?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="delaney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="delaney" href="/user/show/6270594-delaney">delaney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481440240" href="/book/show/24885677-wolf-speaker">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6270594-delaney?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer230425814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5396682570980349874"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550440786ra/27081370.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It is so cozy reading these books. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550440786ra/27081369.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Wolf-Speaker</i> is one of those books you can just grab a blanket, grab a drink, seat yourself in a comfy chair and curl up to a good read. <br/><br/>This reread around, I actually loved it more than the first time around. I probably like it more than the first?! I loved how Tamora Pierce alluded to global warming, pollution, deforestation, chemical dumping, and endangered species. She also played around with the idea of grayness as humans can be both monsters and human and</span>
  <span id="freeText5396682570980349874" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550440786ra/27081370.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It is so cozy reading these books. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550440786ra/27081369.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Wolf-Speaker</i> is one of those books you can just grab a blanket, grab a drink, seat yourself in a comfy chair and curl up to a good read. <br><br>This reread around, I actually loved it more than the first time around. I probably like it more than the first?! I loved how Tamora Pierce alluded to global warming, pollution, deforestation, chemical dumping, and endangered species. She also played around with the idea of grayness as humans can be both monsters and human and monsters can be both human and monsters. It was very intriguing and I suppose little me just did not pick up on that. <br><br>Sadly, Numair doesn't appear a lot in this book. :( I was like--<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550442202ra/27081474.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The entire time. <br><br>I felt more chemistry between them though. (I love slow-burn and yes, age difference is strange but somehow it works because of Daine's maturity/growth...more on that soon.) Because they weren't together the entire book you get to see a lot of Daine by herself and how much Numair cares for her and how much she cares for him in return. <br><br><b>Daine on main was SO GOOD.</b> It's been a year since the last book (she's 14 1/2 now) and she really stays loyal, stays stubborn, and stays moral. She is hard on herself and there were points she did breakdown and felt all the pressure that rode on her shoulder. I especially liked that she is more confident at leading the animals and people as it really showed her overall maturity. She was my childhood hero and still is. I love how caring she is and how she fights her way through. No matter what. <br><br>Her growth in character is also seen in how she handles her Wild Magic abilities. She is able to become part of an animal and follow with them through the animals eyes and some shape-shifting abilities. Whenever she joined with an animal, you can really feel like you were that animal and really see through that animals eyes. It was breathtaking to read. <br><br>Interestingly enough, I found there were a couple subtle plot-lines that were present in the first book but was brought up again in this one. <br>1) Her father who is in the first book is some man with antlers. There is mention of his name in this book, but I want some more confirmations and information!<br>2) Orzone and the Immortals (I mean that's what the quartet is called!) that already started in the first book so I feel like it follows throughout the series. (shoutout to <b>one</b> stone-eating friend, Tkaa)<br>3) Slow-burn romance. (Aww yeah)<br><br>Some honorable Numair mentions:<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>~Numair turning to stone. Breaking the spell. And then asking to be turned to stone again because he's a magic nerd. <br>~Numair turning his "friend" to a tree. <br>~Numair getting really rash and angry at the barrier because he wanted to see Daine on the other side of it. <br>~The animals calling him "Stork Man" (they already approve of him and Daine) <br>~Daine stargazing at Numair's tower....so they stargaze together? Do they sleep in the same place?<br>~Numair telling the Innkeeper he specifically wanted <i>adjoining rooms</i> with a door <i>locked</i> in between them... like he isn't already falling for her.<br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I AM SO PUMPED FOR THE NEXT BOOK. (PLEASEHAVESOMEMORENUMAIRDAINEINTERACTIONSKAYTHANKSBYE.)</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5396682570980349874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer14846522469418125840">This one held up less well for me. It's not bad, it's just sort of... uninteresting? I feel like it's this series' "Woman who Rides Like a Man." I like a lot of the elements, but something doesn't come together. I do like how morality is treated in this one. And I like Maura. But I almost feel like this one has too many convenient allies. And it features Daine being alone with very few of the familiar characters for too long. The pack themselves aren't that interesting to me. I do like Tkaa and </span>
  <span id="freeText14846522469418125840" style="display:none">This one held up less well for me. It's not bad, it's just sort of... uninteresting? I feel like it's this series' "Woman who Rides Like a Man." I like a lot of the elements, but something doesn't come together. I do like how morality is treated in this one. And I like Maura. But I almost feel like this one has too many convenient allies. And it features Daine being alone with very few of the familiar characters for too long. The pack themselves aren't that interesting to me. I do like Tkaa and Kitten, but they don't really carry a book. Plus, minor plot thing, but I thought Jonathan had no close relatives other than Roger, and that was why it was such a huge problem if he died without an heir. Why is Yolanthe so convinced she'll be Queen then? <br /><br />I do continue to like Daine and Numair's dynamic. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Which goes some way to explaining why they sort of work for me as a couple? Mostly this feels like a book where Daine learned to shape-shift, because she's going to need to. And she learned the virtue of tolerance. But other than that...</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abi (The Knights Who Say Book)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abi (The Knights Who Say Book)" href="/user/show/39496028-abi-the-knights-who-say-book">Abi (The Knights Who Say Book)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780679882893" href="/book/show/858665.Wolf_Speaker">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39496028-abi-the-knights-who-say-book?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39496028-abi-the-knights-who-say-book?shelf=read-multiple-times">read-multiple-times</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39496028-abi-the-knights-who-say-book?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2391880617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3018320424840868304">I think my reread of this series has been garnering 5 star ratings because they're just... so easy. They're so comfortable, you know? They're fun but not complicated, layered but not long. I've read them before so I have an idea of what's coming, but it was long enough ago that there are still surprises.<br/><br/>I'd misremembered how soon Daine learns to do different things with her powers, and completely forgotten some things about the immortals. And Maura, sorry, I didn't remember you even existed. So </span>
  <span id="freeText3018320424840868304" style="display:none">I think my reread of this series has been garnering 5 star ratings because they're just... so easy. They're so comfortable, you know? They're fun but not complicated, layered but not long. I've read them before so I have an idea of what's coming, but it was long enough ago that there are still surprises.<br /><br />I'd misremembered how soon Daine learns to do different things with her powers, and completely forgotten some things about the immortals. And Maura, sorry, I didn't remember you even existed. So I was right to think I was due for a reread, and I enjoyed it more than I remembered. The layers about the immortals sometimes being dangerous but other times needing to be given a chance to show who they are is really good. Daine being so determined and spunky but not knowing everything yet is fun. I can even almost like Numair when I try hard to forget where the story goes with him.<br /><br />I will definitely continue to reread!</span>

    <a title="Stephanie Jobe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7984922-stephanie-jobe"><img alt="Stephanie Jobe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571890562p2/7984922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/322762190?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie Jobe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie Jobe" href="/user/show/7984922-stephanie-jobe">Stephanie Jobe</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer322762190" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12713447696652780126">I think a disturbing amount of my psychology could be traced back to Tamora Pierce, most of it from The Song of the Lioness quartet, but then you come to things like oh my absolute obsession with wolves for years of my life. Daine is growing in her confidence and the gods of the People, animals, are becoming even more involved in her life. Not only does this book provide you with a great adventure but it also teaches two lessons. One lesson is about respect for the natural world in a way that go</span>
  <span id="freeText12713447696652780126" style="display:none">I think a disturbing amount of my psychology could be traced back to Tamora Pierce, most of it from The Song of the Lioness quartet, but then you come to things like oh my absolute obsession with wolves for years of my life. Daine is growing in her confidence and the gods of the People, animals, are becoming even more involved in her life. Not only does this book provide you with a great adventure but it also teaches two lessons. One lesson is about respect for the natural world in a way that goes above and beyond even the respect encouraged in the other stories about Daine. The other lesson is about prejudice, not too surprising from an author with such against the grain strong female characters, but she does show it particularly well and it makes her entire world that much more dimensional.<br /><br />(This is the second book of The Immortals quartet, a Tortall series.)</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CqS23610WHZDg7ESwViq3+YZgJFCqs5BtrPjDnEnJrq2WEYPzgiBBYRS5gmkv8j1Hk1gVK7i17QFZc66BsNteA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wyvYcRsrSfEjK/H5fAbL+DfCXea1Toz+CsDEgs5zFd5/1yiheFeQguT6puIZ4anSz5a9I1kGlQu5Fuk2uZdeHA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8596.Tamora_Pierce">About Tamora Pierce</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9005368358864537381">Hey, folks! I just discovered that apparently I have given some very popular books single-star ratings--except I haven't. How do I know I haven't? Because I haven't read those books at all. So before you go getting all hacked off at me for trashing your favorites, know that I've written GoodReads to find out what's going on.<br/><br/>I return to my regularly scheduled profile:<br/>Though I would love to join gro</span>
  <span id="freeText9005368358864537381" style="display:none">Hey, folks! I just discovered that apparently I have given some very popular books single-star ratings--except I haven't. How do I know I haven't? Because I haven't read those books at all. So before you go getting all hacked off at me for trashing your favorites, know that I've written GoodReads to find out what's going on.<br /><br />I return to my regularly scheduled profile:<br />Though I would love to join groups, I'm going to turn them all down. I just don't have the time to take part, so please don't be offended if I don't join your group or accept an invitation. I'm not snooty--I'm just up to my eyeballs in work and appearances!<br /><br />Also, don't be alarmed by the number of books I've read. When I get bored, I go through the different lists and rediscover books I've read in the past. It's a very evil way to use up time when I should be doing other things. Obviously, I've read a lot of books in 54 years!<br /><br />I was born in South Connellsville, PA. My mother wanted to name me "Tamara" but the nurse who filled out my birth certificate misspelled it as "Tamora". When I was 8 my family moved to California, where we lived for 6 years on both sides of the San Francisco peninsula.<br /><br />I started writing stories in 6th grade. My interest in fantasy and science fiction began when I was introduced to ‘The Lord of the Rings’ by J. R. R. Tolkien and so I started to write the kind of books that I was reading. After my parents divorced, my mother took my sisters and me back to Pennsylvania in 1969. There I went to Albert Gallatin Senior High for 2 years and Uniontown Area Senior High School for my senior year.<br /><br />After graduating from the University of Pennsylvania, I wrote the book that became The Song of the Lioness fantasy quartet. I sold some articles and 2 short stories and wrote reviews for a martial arts movie magazine. At last the first book of the quartet, Alanna: The First Adventure was published by Atheneum Books in 1983.<br /><br />Tim Liebe, who became my Spouse-Creature, and I lived in New York City with assorted cats and two parakeets from 1982 - 2006. In 2006 we moved to Syracuse, New York, where we live now with assorted cats, a number of squirrels, birds, raccoons, skunks, opossums, and woodchucks visiting our very small yard. As of 2011, I have 27 novels in print, one short story collection, one comic book arc ("White Tiger: A Hero's Compulsion") co-written with Tim, and a short story anthology co-editing credit. There's more to come, including a companion book to the Tortall `verse. So stay tuned!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9005368358864537381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
